  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f69de37f-74bc-42c4-9298-b15951de8d32'
      });
    }

Still, considering her limited options, she gamely takes up the challenge of running the kennel. And as Rachel starts finding new homes for the abandoned strays, it turns out that it might not just be the dogs that need rescuing.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/301027994" />
    <a title="Tanja (Tanychy) St. Delphi/James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4465641-tanja-tanychy-st-delphi-james"><img alt="Tanja (Tanychy) St. Delphi/James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330431599p2/4465641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/301027994?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanja (Tanychy) St. Delphi/James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanja (Tanychy) St. Delphi/James" href="/user/show/4465641-tanja-tanychy-st-delphi-james">Tanja (Tanychy) St. Delphi/James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4465641-tanja-tanychy-st-delphi-james?shelf=my-little-library">my-little-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4465641-tanja-tanychy-st-delphi-james?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer301027994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15242315511419772527">This is one really sweet and readable story, so 4 stars from me. Just for the record I'm not chick-lit fan at all, so when I give it 4 stars it's really good. Besides I'm dog-lover so I couldn't give it any less. I guess people who like sweet, chick-lit stories will love this one. <br/><br/>This is story about people who try to live their everyday life, but they still don't know that their lives will be changed. It's about women, Rachel, in here late 30's who loses everything and gets everything in the sa</span>
  <span id="freeText15242315511419772527" style="display:none">This is one really sweet and readable story, so 4 stars from me. Just for the record I'm not chick-lit fan at all, so when I give it 4 stars it's really good. Besides I'm dog-lover so I couldn't give it any less. I guess people who like sweet, chick-lit stories will love this one. <br /><br />This is story about people who try to live their everyday life, but they still don't know that their lives will be changed. It's about women, Rachel, in here late 30's who loses everything and gets everything in the same time. She just need to realize that. After her aunt dies she inherits her house and dog shelter. Rachel moves form London and tries to take care about everything. There he'll meet Natalie and Johnny, young couple who are trying to have a child and Zoe also, young divorced women, mother of two sons, who is still struggling after divorce. Although, Rachel thinks he is not right person for this and she tries to find a way to leave all that and find herself, she slowly gets into routine. Where she finds answers on some of the questions. <br /><br />From the blurb you can see how this story will goes, not everything but most of the things. Even though this story is predictable, I can say that I enjoyed. Really, nice read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15242315511419772527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_79920098" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79920098" />
    <a title="Chloe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/591554-chloe"><img alt="Chloe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593904084p2/591554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79920098?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chloe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chloe" href="/user/show/591554-chloe">Chloe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79920098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15140775293903569244">Rachel is a bit horrified when she finds out that her Aunt Dot has died and left her entire estate to her. Dot’s legacy is a boarding kennels in the middle of nowhere, a huge house and a lot of debts to go with it, and Rachel doesn’t much fancy moving and becoming at one with the dogs and their owners. However, when she arrives, she finds the people are nice folk with hearts of gold, and that the dogs quickly grow on you as well. Rachel soon begins to make friends with George, the dishy local ve</span>
  <span id="freeText15140775293903569244" style="display:none">Rachel is a bit horrified when she finds out that her Aunt Dot has died and left her entire estate to her. Dot’s legacy is a boarding kennels in the middle of nowhere, a huge house and a lot of debts to go with it, and Rachel doesn’t much fancy moving and becoming at one with the dogs and their owners. However, when she arrives, she finds the people are nice folk with hearts of gold, and that the dogs quickly grow on you as well. Rachel soon begins to make friends with George, the dishy local vet; Zoe, a single mum of 2 young boys struggling to cope with them and new puppy Toffee; Natalie and Johhny, a couple who subsitute a baby for a dog for the time-being whilst they hide a painful secret, and of course Megan who helped Dot run the whole show. Will Rachel be able to settle down and mend her lonely heart once and for all?<br /><br />I read and adored Lucy’s debut novel The Ballroom Class when it was released last year, and I’ve been really eager for her to bring a second book out! When I found it was about dogs, I was a bit unsure as I’m not the biggest dog lover in the world, but the cover won me over with its lovely winter setting, and I think it’s going to be a big seller in the run up to Christmas. The book is published on 26th November, and it’s one that will be worth the wait and is perfect for the cold winter nights… the book made it onto our Winter Warmers list even before we had reviewed it!<br /><br />Anyway, back to the book. It begins with a narrative by a dog, which was interesting and not at all what I had expected. Soon after though, the book begins with Rachel at the solicitor’s office finding out that she’s inherited the kennels from her Aunt. If I’m honest, I did find the start of the book to be a little bit slow-going and I did wonder how it was going to pan out for the rest of the book. I did of course stick with it and I’m glad I did because it definitely picks up as it gathers momentum, and by the end I was hooked once more. I do wonder if I didn’t get into it at first because as I say, I don’t especially love dogs and therefore the subject matter wasn’t one I was too fussed about reading about, but either way, it did get better for me.<br /><br />The characterisation in the book was fantastic. Rachel was a great character and I liked her very much, but for some reason I kept thinking of her as a twenty-something rather than the 40 year old she was! She doesn’t come across in that way, but it doesn’t make it too problematic for me when I was reading it. However, it was the other characters in the book that I liked best. Zoe, the single mum of 2 was my favourite – her ex-husband was written so horribly you can’t help by feel sorry for her and I liked her progression as the book moved forward. Natalie and Johnny were also such a likeable couple, and the storyline between them was so touching and emotional, it was so well done by Lucy and I congratulate her for tackling such a difficult storyline with real compassion for her characters. Their friend Bill was a good male character although I would have liked to have seen more from him, and the other man in the book is George the vet who I also really liked.<br /><br />One thing that I really enjoyed about this book was how I could picture in my mind the village they lived in, the kennels, Zoe’s house and all the other places mentioned in the book. Dillon has a real knack for descriptive writing – not the sort that goes on and on and ends up boring the reader a little bit, but she weaves it effortlessly through the story so you’re imagining it with every word you read and it unfolds perfectly as the book progresses. I loved her descriptions of the dogs, and the little letters “written” by the dogs to prospective owners were very emotional and well done. You can tell Dillon has a passion for dogs, and this really comes across throughout the whole book.<br /><br />It is a wonderful read, and definitely a nice one for the winter nights if only for that glorious cover but I still find that the beginning really did hinder my enjoyment towards the start which was a shame. It did drag on a little bit and took a while for me to get into the characters but once I did, I thoroughly enjoyed. There are a lot of complex issues wrapped up in the book which are written very emotively, and all of them relevant to society today and I enjoyed how everything felt realistic and didn’t feel like it was going to be rushed to the typical happy ending. I loved the characters, and think Dillon did a great job of making the reader care not only about the humans in the book but the canine ones too :) Definitely one to pick up if you can, I really enjoyed it – it’s gentle, charming and a lovely read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15140775293903569244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8365176054770989982"> The world of canine rescue is the foundation for this sweet story. There are three main vignettes with some minor characters revolving around them. A couple dealing with infertility, a divorced mom of two with the ex from hell and all the attendant heartache and a single career woman, suddenly finding herself without a job.<br/> All find each other when they become involved with a local rescue kennel. Friendships aren't immediate but start slowly, with each so absorbed with their issues that they ca</span>
  <span id="freeText8365176054770989982" style="display:none"> The world of canine rescue is the foundation for this sweet story. There are three main vignettes with some minor characters revolving around them. A couple dealing with infertility, a divorced mom of two with the ex from hell and all the attendant heartache and a single career woman, suddenly finding herself without a job.<br /> All find each other when they become involved with a local rescue kennel. Friendships aren't immediate but start slowly, with each so absorbed with their issues that they can't see what is just beyond their noses. Of course, the dogs do the heavy lifting in getting the characters to start seeing and resolving their issues.<br /> As is usual with animal based stories, the dogs steal the show, especially(for me) Bertie the Basset Hound. And there is plenty of good information about the benefits of rescuing versus buying a dog and some training tips. And there was a twist or two that keep the reader guessing. A quick and sweet read.<br /> <br /> </span>

<div id="review_1525209384" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1525209384" />
    <a title="Tânia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5180979-t-nia"><img alt="Tânia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420673549p2/5180979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1525209384?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tânia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tânia" href="/user/show/5180979-t-nia">Tânia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">dog lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5180979-t-nia?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1525209384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3768897309679805606"><i>“Until one has loved an animal a part of one’s soul remains unawakened.”</i> - Anatole France<br/><br/>What a pleasant, nostalgic read! These lost dogs were the perfect companionship to my lonely heart and they totally stole the show. Don’t get me wrong, I love’em crazy, independent felines, but I’ll always be a dog person at heart. <br/><br/>Oh yes, it’s a slow burner but those are often the best because somewhere along the line you get caught up in the story and you don’t let go till it’s finished. For me it was when</span>
  <span id="freeText3768897309679805606" style="display:none"><i>“Until one has loved an animal a part of one’s soul remains unawakened.”</i> - Anatole France<br /><br />What a pleasant, nostalgic read! These lost dogs were the perfect companionship to my lonely heart and they totally stole the show. Don’t get me wrong, I love’em crazy, independent felines, but I’ll always be a dog person at heart. <br /><br />Oh yes, it’s a slow burner but those are often the best because somewhere along the line you get caught up in the story and you don’t let go till it’s finished. For me it was when these three different stories started to connect through dog whispering. All the characters are so likable you can’t help but to feel empathy towards them and their dilemmas. Plus, the portrayal of the animals is so genuine it pulls at your heart strings… and how could it not? <br /><br />Rachel &amp; George – Rachel's growth was noteworthy throughout the story and I really enjoyed the way their romance unfolded even though it was anything but conventional. They were both mature and pondered people. Plus Gem. <br /><br />Nat &amp; Johnny –I admit at first I wasn’t that into the whole getting pregnant obsession of Nat’s. And Johnny didn’t seem that into it either. But then things took a turn and I felt for them. I’m so glad the author didn’t go all cliché on them in the end, though. Plus Bertie. <br /><br />Zoe &amp; Bill – The couple who made me smile the most from the way they met till the inevitable <i>I’m a single mother</i> talk. Plus Toffee and Lulu. <br /><br />The only thing I thought could’ve been handled better was Dot’s mystery which wasn’t that shocking. Honestly I was expecting something in the lines of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i>“I gave up my own child to be raised by my sister”</i>. Now that would go along well with Dot and Rachel’s shared looks and the inheritance left to her, wouldn’t it? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But to be honest, that was minor. I was much more invested in lost dogs warming up lonely hearts and vice versa. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3768897309679805606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1471258796">
  <td colspan="2">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155567236?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425238875" href="/book/show/9276237-lost-dogs-and-lonely-hearts">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one, sadly.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/276143-linda?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/276143-linda?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/276143-linda?shelf=guilty-pleasures">guilty-pleasures</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155567236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11141385819376350062">Woman goes to take over dead aunt's dog rescue legacy, woman meets dog, woman meets vet. Lost Dogs and Lonely Hearts is well-written and incredibly predictable - which isn't terrible, in a book that is meant to be tear-jerkingly heartwarming. People who like dogs and love stories will inevitably enjoy this.<br/><br/>However, the nature of the mystery at the core of the book -- why her aunt lived as she did -- makes me see red. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Ultimately, the aunt rejects marriage to the "perfect man" becau</span></span>
  <span id="freeText11141385819376350062" style="display:none">Woman goes to take over dead aunt's dog rescue legacy, woman meets dog, woman meets vet. Lost Dogs and Lonely Hearts is well-written and incredibly predictable - which isn't terrible, in a book that is meant to be tear-jerkingly heartwarming. People who like dogs and love stories will inevitably enjoy this.<br /><br />However, the nature of the mystery at the core of the book -- why her aunt lived as she did -- makes me see red. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ultimately, the aunt rejects marriage to the "perfect man" because he turns out to be bisexual and can't give up male liaisons on the side. "Bisexual men can't be faithful or truly commit" is a horrible stereotype that the world would be better off without. It's not true, and it's hurtful, and seeing this book mindlessly reinforce that made me want to rip it up. Shame on you, Lucy Dillon. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie Mole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie Mole" href="/user/show/57372902-melanie-mole">Melanie Mole</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2017491404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7930524187327571577">What a genuinely lovely book this is.<br/><br/>I hadn't read any of Lucy Dillon's books before, but I will now!<br/><br/>The story centres around Rachel who inherits a large house, kennels, friends, and the responsibility for her rescue dogs from Dot, her unusual aunt. <br/><br/>Prior to this Rachel had only know the trendy London scene where her job in PR, her interest in fashion, and hours spent networking left little room for anything else, except the odd evening spent with a man who turns out to be married. <br/><br/>After her mov</span>
  <span id="freeText7930524187327571577" style="display:none">What a genuinely lovely book this is.<br /><br />I hadn't read any of Lucy Dillon's books before, but I will now!<br /><br />The story centres around Rachel who inherits a large house, kennels, friends, and the responsibility for her rescue dogs from Dot, her unusual aunt. <br /><br />Prior to this Rachel had only know the trendy London scene where her job in PR, her interest in fashion, and hours spent networking left little room for anything else, except the odd evening spent with a man who turns out to be married. <br /><br />After her move to the country, and not being a dog person, Rachel finds it all a bit daunting. But with Megan, the kennel manager's help, she settles into the daily task list, eventually even seeming to enjoy it.<br /><br />One dog in particular takes to her her. Not really surprising as it was Gem her aunt Dot's dog. Their relationship grows alongside Rachel's confidence. She finds abilities she never new that she has. <br />Even daring to look start looking forward instead of back. <br /><br />An unexpected turn in the story sees Rachel with a new man entering her life, as well as a new challenge. <br /><br />Rachel gets the chance to start to make her relationship with her mother better because of her new challenges. She also finds out a family secret along the way.<br /><br />As soon as I started reading this book I loved it. I didn't want to put it down. Snatching little moments for a few more pages as I went through my day. Splendid!</span>

<div id="review_437273428" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/437273428" />
    <a title="Valen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5566820-valen"><img alt="Valen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529467392p2/5566820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/437273428?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valen" href="/user/show/5566820-valen">Valen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5566820-valen?shelf=will-read-again">will-read-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer437273428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14998910884532987981"> I L.O.V.E. this book!!! It's cute, it's quirky, it's funny, it's real; it's the kind of book that tugs at your heartstrings and with all the D.O.G.S. involve, it's just plain amazing!<br/><br/> First character we meet is Rachel. She just inherited her Aunt Dot's estate where a kennel is included along with rescued dogs. She just got out from a bad relationship and lost her job at the same time. <br/><br/> Rachel had a 10-year relationship with her married boss, Oliver, who in my opinion tricked her into having a r</span>
  <span id="freeText14998910884532987981" style="display:none"> I L.O.V.E. this book!!! It's cute, it's quirky, it's funny, it's real; it's the kind of book that tugs at your heartstrings and with all the D.O.G.S. involve, it's just plain amazing!<br /><br /> First character we meet is Rachel. She just inherited her Aunt Dot's estate where a kennel is included along with rescued dogs. She just got out from a bad relationship and lost her job at the same time. <br /><br /> Rachel had a 10-year relationship with her married boss, Oliver, who in my opinion tricked her into having a relationship with him. At first, I was a bit put off with her because I can't help but think that she's a bad person being in a relationship with a married guy. But then I realize, reading more, that maybe she was a "victim" here. Being lied at by her boss-lover that he was no longer sleeping with his wife and that he feels unloved. But then I also have this argument with myself that she should've known better to saddle off with a married man. Anyway, it took her a while to realize that she didn't deserve that kind of treatment and that it wasn't right what she was doing. And am happy for her that she's the one who broke it off. <br /><br /> There was this heartbreaking scene where the wife, Kath, visited her at the kennels and she made it seem like Rachel was just a distraction to her husband nothing more nothing less. I can't say that Rachel deserve that but I guess that was punishment enough for her. I felt sorry for Rachel and it felt as if she got the bad end of the whole situation. Here, I came to the conclusion that people make bad choices and some way or the other we have to face the consequences of the choices we make, move one, and hope that you could forget and try to continue with your life provided that you won't make the same mistake again. Which in this story was what Rachel was trying to do. And there was Gem,the collie, I think somehow he helped Rachel figure out everything in the end being her companion and a loyal friend. <br /><br /> There's also this situation in the end involving George the vet. How glad I was that Rachel chose him and not that no-good boss of hers. She wavered a bit in the end but she realized what she really wanted and that's not with Oliver. And I got this feeling that even if she did go back with Oliver, she would have realized sooner or later that it's not going to work out and that she'll eventually go back to Longhampton. <br /><br /> We also met Natalie and Johnny who were trying to have a baby. They've been trying for years but nothing has come of it and at some point Natalie became desperate. Always checking her temperatures, doing all sorts of tests for herself. At some point, Natalie and Johnny came to an agreement that they're going have to have tests to see if they both were capable of having a baby. Something went wrong with Johnny's test and it all seemed to fall apart from that moment on. <br /><br /> I can't even imagine how sad it must've been for the both of them after the doctor told them the test results, especially Johnny's. It's not anybody's fault but there was a point in the story that they both don't know how to cope with the fact that maybe they can never have a baby. And maybe, they didn't communicate well enough to tell each other what they want and what they're feeling. It's not until the end that they realize that whatever happens, as long as they have each other, everything will be okay. And it's not like they really can't have a baby. They are options out there to choose from. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I like the scene where Johnny wouldn't agree of a donor's sperm. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I think it was cute of him to not want that and be all possessive of Natalie. I like that scene and until the end, he was still thinking of Nat. And then there's Bertie, the basset hound, who I think gave them that extra push to hold on to each other and not give up. How glad I am that they all worked it out in the end. <br /><br /> Next one is Zoe, single mother of two adorable little boys, Spencer and Leo. Her story definitely tugged at my heartstrings. Left by her husband to be with his colleague from work, she's been raising her sons for a year now. Can't help but think that this kind of situation happens a lot nowadays and it's nothing new. But the way that she handles everything and being a strong mother for her two children is just admirable. And with everything that's happened especially with the way Spencer is reacting with the whole situation. I guess that's a normal reaction from a seven-year-old. <br /><br /> She faltered a bit and there was that time that she got a little hysterical after having Toffee, the labrador pup, but she never gave up. She got through with all of it, no thanks to her self-centered husband. And she had help too of course, which shows that nobody gets through life without a little help. And how could I forget the blooming romance between her and Dr. Bill. It was sweet and I'm glad that she came to an understanding with her children in the end.<br /><br /> There was also a secret involving Rachel's Aunt Dot and what a shock it was for me actually; it was totally unexpected. But this little bit of information was maybe one of the reason that Rachel realized that there's something more from taking care of abandoned dogs. She learned acceptance and how to move one with her life despite the fact of having a bad past. I guess you could say that there's some similarities with Rachel's situation to the dogs'. In the end, they're given a chance to start over and be happy. <br /><br /> I hoped that Megan had a bit of romance going on for her. I like her and let's face it, Rachel couldn't do it without Megan. There's also Freda and Ted who helped work the kennels as well. They all came together made this book as animated as it can be. I actually thought that with all the characters involve, it was hard to keep track of the story. How wrong was I in that front. The friendship formed between this characters was what made the story believable and real.<br /><br /> In the end, I was very happy to have read this book. This was the first Lucy Dillon that I've read and I'm happy to say that I'll be reading more from her in the future. ♥ ♥ ♥ ♥ ♥ :D<br /><br /> <br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14998910884532987981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/250159680" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3437180-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504386937p2/3437180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/250159680?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/3437180-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer250159680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1725037023135743014">An excellent feel good book that will renew all your faith in romance and love!<br/><br/>Rachel, nearly 40, and fresh out of a long relationship as mistress to the love of her life, has come to the country to sort out her inheritance from Aunt, a dogs home!!<br/>Just wanting to pay the tax and run with the rest to sort out her complicated life, Rachel finds herself not only getting involved with the rehoming of such delightful doggies as Bertie the Basset Hound and Lulu the Poodle, but with the locals too...an</span>
  <span id="freeText1725037023135743014" style="display:none">An excellent feel good book that will renew all your faith in romance and love!<br /><br />Rachel, nearly 40, and fresh out of a long relationship as mistress to the love of her life, has come to the country to sort out her inheritance from Aunt, a dogs home!!<br />Just wanting to pay the tax and run with the rest to sort out her complicated life, Rachel finds herself not only getting involved with the rehoming of such delightful doggies as Bertie the Basset Hound and Lulu the Poodle, but with the locals too...and a tangle with the gorgeous vet winds up with her more tangled than she thought!<br />There is single mum Zoe, struggling to housetrain her two sons let alone the puppy her ex lands on her - thank goodness she can turn to chirpy Aussie Megan, kennel maid at the Dogs Home and if dishy doctor Bill wants to lend a hand too....<br />Then there are Nat and Johnny, desperate for a baby but meanwhile who better to nurture their parental impulses but Bertie the Basset Hound...a delightful cast of characters that just make the story flow and whom you cannot help cheering on and loving! Settle down for a jolly romp of a read that will have you chuckling and feeling just great!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1725037023135743014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9617672-stephanie-a?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9617672-stephanie-a?shelf=animals">animals</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer372027843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2894617616015720912">For once, neither the title nor the cover lied. After a slightly slow start it was full of dogs, dogs with names and personalities, dogs who were the most important characters and made all the connections between people. As a result, I even liked the people. Probably because it was also full of romance and pending babies (but not actual babies), yet nothing explicit to offend my delicate sensibilities. This is the best animal book for adults I have ever read. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3135007897&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3135007897" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13381049971429656925">The story started out well but once author revealed that the heroine had been having an affair with a married man for the last seven years, I was done. Sorry... adultery is wrong. It’s not sexy or dramatic; it’s dishonest, cowardly, and cruel. The sympathy I initially felt for her when it sounded like her boyfriend had cheated on her was gone once I learned she was his mistress. Too bad... I thought I had found a new author.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

I loved all the dogs in this book and the main characters felt like real people. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17014899470301499776">If you need a happy ending, laughter inducing, doggy loving sort of story I highly recommend you try Lost Dogs and Lonely Hearts. <br/><br/>What a well told, heart-warming story! I wasn't sure in beginning, but it quickly became the story I was hoping for. The one you reread on a rainy day when you need a pick me up. Something easy but fulfilling. The best part was that I listened to it as an audio. If I had started reading a physical copy, I would have picked up from the lingo that it took place in Engla</span>
  <span id="freeText17014899470301499776" style="display:none">If you need a happy ending, laughter inducing, doggy loving sort of story I highly recommend you try Lost Dogs and Lonely Hearts. <br /><br />What a well told, heart-warming story! I wasn't sure in beginning, but it quickly became the story I was hoping for. The one you reread on a rainy day when you need a pick me up. Something easy but fulfilling. The best part was that I listened to it as an audio. If I had started reading a physical copy, I would have picked up from the lingo that it took place in England. But, I wouldn't have experienced it the same way that the narrator allowed me to. She had a lovely voice, and I hope she reads the other Lucy Dillon books on audio. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17014899470301499776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172201317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13698447204441058698">Lost Dogs and Lonely Hearts is the first book I have read by Lucy Dillon. I was given this book to read by a client and on first glimpse I liked the look of the book, girly pink and white with glitter snow balls on the front. It looks like your typical chic lit book and then came the title of the book and this put me off. I am not really what you would call your typical animal lover and I would defiantly not put a book about dogs on the top of my to read list. All this aside I had run out of boo</span>
  <span id="freeText13698447204441058698" style="display:none">Lost Dogs and Lonely Hearts is the first book I have read by Lucy Dillon. I was given this book to read by a client and on first glimpse I liked the look of the book, girly pink and white with glitter snow balls on the front. It looks like your typical chic lit book and then came the title of the book and this put me off. I am not really what you would call your typical animal lover and I would defiantly not put a book about dogs on the top of my to read list. All this aside I had run out of books to read so I thought I would give it a go. <br /><br /><br />**Plot** <br /><br />The book opens with the lovely Rachel whose life in London is falling to bits loosing her job, flat and her heart is breaking. Rachel's aunt Dot has past away leaving her home, Kennels and her dog Gem to Rachel. Rachel is not what you would call a dog lover with her London lifestyle. As Rachel starts working with the Kennels and starts to help Megan who runs the Kennels to re-home the rescue dogs, matching them up with perfect owners. She must make a decision if to stay in Dots house and carry on running the Kennels ,or to sell up for a nice tidy profit and head back to her life in London. <br /><br />The book weaves in new characters as the book goes on. We meet Natalie and Johnny, a married couple who are desperately trying for children with no avail. We also meet Zoe who works full time and looks after her two children Leo and Spencer and is finding things very difficult when her ex husband decides to give their children a Labrador puppy. Also we meet single Bill the doctor friend of Natalie and Johnny who is matched up with his perfect dog but one he didn't expect! <br /><br /><br />**Opinion** <br /><br />This book is a well written book once you get half way through. The first half of the book is quite slow and I did at a couple of points think about just putting it down. It certainly didn't grip me from the first page. However I am so glad I carried on as the second half of the book was brilliant. The way Lucy writes about Rachel makes you really warm to her and you want to see her happy. It is not the best book when it came to trying to bring in the characters together. It felt like I was reading three separate mini books and then it was all thrown together which was a shame as in the last half of the book when the characters are all together the book is endearing. It was unusual to read about a different relationship which was between man and their four legged furry friends. <br /><br /><br />Also on my book blog <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reabookreview.blogspot.com/">http://reabookreview.blogspot.com/</a>. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13698447204441058698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152095951?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookaholics" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookaholics" href="/user/show/1554860-bookaholics">Bookaholics</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425238875" href="/book/show/9276237-lost-dogs-and-lonely-hearts">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152095951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14087513285702197455">Lost Dogs and Lonely Hearts by Lucy Dillon<br/>Contemporary Romance – March 1st, 2011<br/>4 stars<br/><br/>Rachel is heart-broken and disillusioned. She has just had a break up with her boyfriend and lost her job. In addition, she inherited her aunt’s house in the suburbs, a dog rescue operation, and a kennel full of unwanted strays including her aunt’s border collie. When she goes to stay at her aunt’s house to sort out the mess and attempts to sell the house, she ends up delaying her return to London. Before she </span>
  <span id="freeText14087513285702197455" style="display:none">Lost Dogs and Lonely Hearts by Lucy Dillon<br />Contemporary Romance – March 1st, 2011<br />4 stars<br /><br />Rachel is heart-broken and disillusioned. She has just had a break up with her boyfriend and lost her job. In addition, she inherited her aunt’s house in the suburbs, a dog rescue operation, and a kennel full of unwanted strays including her aunt’s border collie. When she goes to stay at her aunt’s house to sort out the mess and attempts to sell the house, she ends up delaying her return to London. Before she knows it, she was staying indefinitely and getting more and more involved in the dog rescue...and the handsome vet that volunteers at the kennel.<br /><br />Natalie and Johnny’s marriage has hit a rough patch ever since they started trying for a baby. Despite their best efforts and countless tries, they remain childless. But the yearning for a child threatens to consume their marriage, Natalie decids to foster a dog for the kennel. Could Bertie, the basset hound salvage their marriage?<br /><br />Meanwhile, Zoe, a single mother with two boys under ten, is recovering from her divorce. Bitter and angry, she is upset when her irresponsible ex-husband gives the kids a puppy. Now she was stuck with training Toffee and cleaning up after its mess, not to mention her own kids! But one thing leads to another and somehow Zoe finds herself meeting another dog owner, the handsome doctor Bill.<br /><br />Lost Dogs and Lonely Hearts is a fun and charming read that feels like an ensemble romantic comedy. It has the right amounts of ‘aww’ moments sprinkled in and loveable characters. (Especially Bertie, the incorrigibly gluttonous Basset Hound, whose antics had me grinning from ear to ear.) The best part is that even though there is a large cast, all the characters feel realistic and relatable. The dogs are in this book act as supporting characters, but sometimes it feels like they steal the show! <br /><br />Heartwarming and engaging, this book is like comfort food for the soul. If you like your romance light and full of touching moments, Lost Dogs and Lonenly Hearts is highly recommended for you.<br /><br />Reviewed by Pauline from the Bookaholics Romance Club<br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Piepie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Piepie " href="/user/show/663327-piepie">Piepie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425238875" href="/book/show/9276237-lost-dogs-and-lonely-hearts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/663327-piepie?shelf=dogs-and-other-animals">dogs-and-other-animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/663327-piepie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120298112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11499787227310445823"><b>Fun story, but overall I wasn't thrilled by it...</b><br/><br/>A slow start at the very beginning, and I considered throwing in the towel. But then the story picked up, as more characters (and more dogs!) were introduced and the novel became a lot more interesting. <br/><br/>I thought Rachel was going to be a "childfree" character ... you don't see many of those in books, it seems, and I love the following quote: "I always say my biological clock must be digital, because I've never heard it ticking." And then on the op</span>
  <span id="freeText11499787227310445823" style="display:none"><b>Fun story, but overall I wasn't thrilled by it...</b><br /><br />A slow start at the very beginning, and I considered throwing in the towel. But then the story picked up, as more characters (and more dogs!) were introduced and the novel became a lot more interesting. <br /><br />I thought Rachel was going to be a "childfree" character ... you don't see many of those in books, it seems, and I love the following quote: "I always say my biological clock must be digital, because I've never heard it ticking." And then on the opposite end of the spectrum poor Natalie was so hung up on the idea of having her own baby. Adoption didn't seem to be an option, as her husband appeared to want "their own" child. In the end both characters seemed to do almost a 180. I'm trying not to be spoiler-y but I think Natalie seemed to be more accepting of the cards they were dealt and she became less whiny :) I'm a little disappointed in Rachel -- if you have a night of drunk sex, what do you think is going to happen? -- and she and her partner could have been a lot more careful.<br /><br />I liked Zoe and I felt so sorry for her as she had to juggle kids, work, ex-husband's new girlfriend, AND a new puppy. Her ex-husband seemed like a real piece of work ... dumping Toffee on her with hardly an explanation and then spending money like it was water. Zoe's son Spencer was a total brat. I liked the references to Doctor Who but in this novel it was spelled "Dr. Who" when everybody knows it's DOCTOR Who.<br /><br />I really liked Megan and I wish there was more to her story. I also loved Dot's backstory and the secrets in the house that Rachel inherited. Rachel seemed to be pretty independent and I liked how after the whole baby thing she still liked her own space and she wanted to do things unconventionally in her own way.<br /><br />Overall, a nice fluffy "dog" story but I think I enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18623990.A_Hundred_Pieces_of_Me" title="A Hundred Pieces of Me by Lucy Dillon" rel="nofollow noopener"> A Hundred Pieces of Me</a> better.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_85179185" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/85179185" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2464996-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1246138510p2/2464996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85179185?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/2464996-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85179185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13233255024337875068">This is the book that won the Romantic Novel of the Year this year, so I hoped it'd be something a bit special. It's chick lit, but chick lit done really, really well - reminded me of Julia Williams or Sarah Duncan whose books I've enjoyed a lot recently. I mean, what's not to like? A large cast of characters - townie Rachel who inherits a kennels and dog rescue centre, a gruff (but attractive) vet, the couple trying to have a baby, the single mum struggling, the Aussie kennel maid, the sexy vil</span>
  <span id="freeText13233255024337875068" style="display:none">This is the book that won the Romantic Novel of the Year this year, so I hoped it'd be something a bit special. It's chick lit, but chick lit done really, really well - reminded me of Julia Williams or Sarah Duncan whose books I've enjoyed a lot recently. I mean, what's not to like? A large cast of characters - townie Rachel who inherits a kennels and dog rescue centre, a gruff (but attractive) vet, the couple trying to have a baby, the single mum struggling, the Aussie kennel maid, the sexy village doctor, and the most wonderful cast of dogs you've ever met, all with their own characters. Gem the collie's to die for, Toffee the labrador pup, but my personal favourite was Bertie the greedy basset hound. I'm not a particularly doggie person, but this book almost converted me. Add to that a few strong love stories and a mystery about the dead aunt and this book has everything. Highly recommended to everyone who sometimes enjoys an escapist read that has nothing to do with great literature but is a lovely way to spend an afternoon, on a sunbed or not.<br /><br />Apologies I can't pass my copy on - really annoyingly, it had 50 pages missing early on and two sections repeated. And even that couldn't spoil my enjoyment...!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer250305093" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10403223136550804128">I'm a sucker for a good dog book and Lucy Dillon's didn't disappoint. I thoroughly enjoyed this story about a 39-year-old woman, Rachel, who inherits a rescue kennel in England just after losing her job and undergoing a break-up. I had never read any of Lucy Dillon's books before but I enjoyed her style of writing. She is very good at drawing readers into a well-developed plot and creating likeable characters that readers can bond with. Add romance, a kennel full of rescue dogs searching for the</span>
  <span id="freeText10403223136550804128" style="display:none">I'm a sucker for a good dog book and Lucy Dillon's didn't disappoint. I thoroughly enjoyed this story about a 39-year-old woman, Rachel, who inherits a rescue kennel in England just after losing her job and undergoing a break-up. I had never read any of Lucy Dillon's books before but I enjoyed her style of writing. She is very good at drawing readers into a well-developed plot and creating likeable characters that readers can bond with. Add romance, a kennel full of rescue dogs searching for their forever home, and you get a book that's hard to put down. I enjoyed this novel so much that I plan to read Dillon's latest book, Walking Back to Happiness, next. If you are a dog lover, and enjoy "smart chick lit," you'll enjoy Lucy Dillon's books! And kudos to Dillon for raising awareness of rescue dogs.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/269978363?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathalie" href="/user/show/7361616-nathalie">Nathalie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269978363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8111929947170483004">Well I think it says it all that I have finished this book in one day! I loved this one as much as the other 2 of Lucy Dillon's that I have read this past week. I have really enjoyed reading about the many residents of Longhampton, and of the town itself - I really feel like I know the place now, I can picture it vividly in my head!<br/>Lucy Dillon brings the town and the characters to life, and with each book, I have really felt like I know the residents, and I can picture all the dogs too. This has</span>
  <span id="freeText8111929947170483004" style="display:none">Well I think it says it all that I have finished this book in one day! I loved this one as much as the other 2 of Lucy Dillon's that I have read this past week. I have really enjoyed reading about the many residents of Longhampton, and of the town itself - I really feel like I know the place now, I can picture it vividly in my head!<br />Lucy Dillon brings the town and the characters to life, and with each book, I have really felt like I know the residents, and I can picture all the dogs too. This has a been a lovely book to read, which has left me feeling happy and I find I am still thinking about the characters now, after finishing it, wondering how they are all getting on.<br />I am very much looking forward to more of Lucy Dillon's books, and I would definitely recommend this and her previous books to everyone.</span>

    <a title="Lynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1195340-lynne"><img alt="Lynne" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142777411?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynne" href="/user/show/1195340-lynne">Lynne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142777411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13523890421444282190">This is another book that has had mixed reviews. The story of Rachel who inherited her aunt's house and rescue kennels. There are separate but connected stories about other characters - Natalie and Johnny who are desperate for a baby, Zoe whose husband has left her for another woman, Bill a confirmed batchelor and then the handsome vet! Through in a few dogs and some romance and you've got a great book. Ok it is a bit predictable, you can tell the ending probably right from the beginning but the</span>
  <span id="freeText13523890421444282190" style="display:none">This is another book that has had mixed reviews. The story of Rachel who inherited her aunt's house and rescue kennels. There are separate but connected stories about other characters - Natalie and Johnny who are desperate for a baby, Zoe whose husband has left her for another woman, Bill a confirmed batchelor and then the handsome vet! Through in a few dogs and some romance and you've got a great book. Ok it is a bit predictable, you can tell the ending probably right from the beginning but the lovely style of the writing and the feel good aura just makes it a good read. I'll definitely be reading more of Lucy Dillon's stuff. Highly recommended but only if you like chicklit!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BRR8YnPKOLpFaXO/RWHJYby9ZeK7wxEy899Jcsf0ZXCyY+O+heBJYxXm8btYqVO14nqrIOIoHkxcE+2arEeC2g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_38605078'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38605078-bokhandeln-p-riverside-drive?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Bokhandeln på Riverside Drive<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/6440338.Frida_Skyb_ck?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Frida Skybäck<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.50 avg rating &mdash; 1,121 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2018\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer11023216654409757442\">Charlotte är för ung för att vara änka, för ung för att förlora den hon älskar. I sitt vilsna tillstånd tar hon en paus från sitt framgångsrika företag och söker ro på den skånska landsbygden. Men så får hon får ett oväntat besked, hon har ärvt ett h<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11023216654409757442\" style=\"display:none\">Charlotte är för ung för att vara änka, för ung för att förlora den hon älskar. I sitt vilsna tillstånd tar hon en paus från sitt framgångsrika företag och söker ro på den skånska landsbygden. Men så får hon får ett oväntat besked, hon har ärvt ett hus i London av en moster hon knappt visste att hon hade. Och huset inrymmer en bokhandel.\nInställd på att sälja huset flyger Charlotte till England, där den konkursfärdiga Riverside Bookshop och den excentriska personalen verkar bortom all räddning. Men trots att Charlotte inte vet något om hur man driver en bokhandel växer snart en gemenskap med den motsträviga personalen fram.\nSamtidigt som Charlotte kämpar för att rädda bokhandeln inser hon att det är något som inte riktigt stämmer. Numera bor hon i Lund med sin man och deras två barn. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14194639069683013317">Lucy Dillon was born in Cumbria, worked for a while in publishing in London, and now lives in the Wye Valley with her husband and their Border terrier. She has written eight novels set in the fictional Midlands town of Longhampton, which looks a bit like Hereford, although the inhabitants tend to sound rather more Northern than that. <br/><br/></span>
